<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">A low-cost compact circularly polarized (CP) directional antenna is proposed for universal ultra-high frequency (UHF) RF identification (RFID) handheld reader applications. The antenna consists of four sequentially rotated inverted-F antennas (IFAs) fed by a compact four-feed network with closed-form design formulas. A prototype is implemented by FR-4 substrates and a thick air layer for the reduction of cost. For return loss (RL) &gt; 13 dB, 3-dB gain variation, and axial ratio (AR) , the prototype achieves the measured bandwidth of 14.9% and exhibits stable symmetrical directional radiation patterns with wide half-power beamwidth. Compared with the reported UHF RFID directional reader antennas, the proposed structure not only exhibits the largest CP bandwidth for easily covering the entire UHF RFID band but also achieves compact size of 95 Ã100 Ã13.6 mm<sup>3</sup>.</div>

<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>RF Identification (RFID) is to paste tags on goods, animals, or people for the purpose of identification and tracking by electromagnetic waves. In recent years, RFID technology has developed rapidly and appeared in many applications, such as logistics transportation, traffic toll collection, asset tracking, employee attendance record, and so on. With the advantages of rapid identification, long-range read-write, high memory capability and high reliability, the ultra-high frequency (UHF) passive RFID is now a preferred technology among all the RFID technologies.</p><p>The reader antenna is one of the key components in RFID systems and has been designed with circularly polarized (CP) operation, because CP waves can avoid severe polarization mismatch and ensure the reliability of communications between readers and tags. Another issue researchers need to consider is that each country has a different frequency for UHF RFID applications and the universal UHF RFID frequency ranges from 840 to 955Â MHz (bandwidth of 12.8%). Therefore, a reader antenna covering the entire UHF RFID frequency would contribute to the development of cost-effective RFID system for worldwide application. In addition, RFID handheld readers should have compact size and directional radiation pattern.</p><p>To achieve CP radiation across the universal UHF RFID band, structure of stacked corner-truncated patches fed by suspended microstrip feed line through four probes was investigated in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>, and then the multi-feed structure was improved by using a horizontally meandered strip feed technique <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. To simplify the structure and design process of the universal UHF RFID reader antenna, the directly-fed single-layer patch with a coplanar parasitic patch and an L-shaped ground was presented in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>. However, the volumes of these universal RFID reader antennas are greater than <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 9.913em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 8.892em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1008.89em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-3" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">250</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-4" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">Ã</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-5" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">250</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-6" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">Ã</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-7" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">36</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-8" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-9"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.68em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-10"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-11"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-12" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.685em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-13" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">250 \times 250 \times 36~\hbox{mm}^3</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, too large to integrate into handheld readers. For the purpose of miniaturization, crossed dipole <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>, tortuous monopole <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>, fractal monopole <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>, and square slot structure <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a> are employed to CP RFID reader antennas. But the disadvantages of these designs are the bidirectional or omnidirectional radiation patterns. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>, slot-loaded circular and square patches fed by L-shaped probe and proximity-fed line are adopted for designing compact directional CP antenna. Nevertheless, the CP bandwidths of these antennas are still narrow.</p><p>Actually, the multi-feed antenna based on a feed network and sequentially rotated elements can achieve larger bandwidth and higher CP performance compared with single-feed technique. A small reader antenna consists of four monopole fed by a series feed network is presented in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a>. Methods of meandered line are applied to both radiating elements and feed network for miniaturization at the expense of small CP bandwidth. Recently, the two-feed antenna using shorted inverted-L radiating elements and shorted inverted-T strip is studied in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a>. But the asymmetric radiating structure deteriorates the axial-ratio (AR) of the antenna. To the best knowledge of the authors, there were no report and literature about the compact CP directional universal UHF RFID antenna for handheld reader applications at present.</p><p>In this letter, we present a compact CP directional antenna with low cost for universal UHF RFID handheld reader applications. The antenna is composed of four sequentially rotated inverted-F antennas (IFAs) fed by a compact four-feed network through four vertical probes. The network is compact by employing a <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-14" role="math" style="width: 2.165em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.92em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-15"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-16"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.44em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-17" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">180</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.441em; left: 1.505em;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-18" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">180^\circ</script></tex-math></inline-formula> out-of-phase power divider <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a> and two miniaturized couplers <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a>. Above all, the schematic and analytical design formulas of the network and configuration of the antenna are presented. Then, a prototype is simulated, fabricated, and measured for verification. To reduce costs, the prototype is implemented by cheap FR-4 substrates and a thick air layer. At last, we compared the design with that of reported UHF RFID directional reader antennas.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Antenna Configuration and Design</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2a"><h3>A. Compact Four-Feed Network</h3><p>The schematic of the compact four-feed network is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>. It consists of a 180Â° out-of-phase power divider and two same miniaturized couplers. All of the characteristic impedances are normalized with respect to the system load impedance of 50 Î©.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/7042302/7042302-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/7042302/7042302-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 1. </b><fig><p>Schematic of the proposed novel compact four-feed network.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7042302/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The out-of-phase power divider is designed by inserting a conductor plate into the mid-layer of a double-sided parallel stripline (DSPSL) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_2a">[12]</a>. Therefore, the RF signal from the input port 1 is divided into two-way of signals with equal amplitude and 180Â° phase difference on the top and bottom microstrip lines. With the advantages of novel compact structure and simple analytic design method, the feed network is well fit to the design of multi-feed CP antennas.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2b"><h3>B. Configuration and Design of the Antenna</h3><p>The configuration and design parameters of the proposed antenna are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Figs.Â 2</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">3</a>. It consists of four sequentially rotated IFAs fed by the novel compact four-feed network in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2a" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ II-A</a>. The radiating patches of the IFAs are printed on subface of the upper substrate with the size of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-547" role="math" style="width: 6.249em; padding-left: 0.243em;">Ã</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-551" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">95</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-552" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-553"><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.685em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-557" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">95 \times 95~\hbox{mm}^2</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Since the patches are inverted, the upper substrate not merely acts as the radome for environmental protection but also enhances the gain of the antenna. The four-feed network is implemented on the middle and bottom substrates with different sizes of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-558" role="math" style="width: 6.249em; <p></p><p>The four-feed network stimulates the IFAs through the four vertical probes. IFA is an evolution of a quarter wavelength monopole. Thus the radiating patch parallel with the conductor plane increases capacitance of antenna. Fortunately, this problem can be solved by employing a shorting pin between the terminal of radiating patch and the conductor plane. Because the shorting pin increases the inductance and maintains the resonance of antenna. The feed probes and shorting pins have identical diameter of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-74-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-901" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.2em 2.465em -999.997em); width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-909" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-74">{{\rm D}_2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> but different heights of (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-75-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-910" role="math" style="width: 4.087em; The air layer with thickness of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-79-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-954" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.2em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-955"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-956"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-957"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-958"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-959"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-960"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-961" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">H</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-962" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-79">{{\rm H}_1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is used for enhancing the gain and bandwidth of antenna. In addition, four circular slots with diameter <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-80-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-963" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; The substrates are fixed by eleven-set of teflon devices, and each of them includes a screw, a nut, and a pillar. display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.9em 2.405em -999.997em); width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-87">~\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are employed at isolation ports of couplers for matching.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/7042302/7042302-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/7042302/7042302-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 4. </b><fig><p>Photos of the protype. (a)Â bottom view. (b)Â top view.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7042302/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/7042302/7042302-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7024204/7042302/7042302-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 5. </b><fig><p>Simulated and measured reflection coefficient of input port, gain, cross polarization, AR at boresight, and measured efficiency of the protype.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7042302/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The return loss (RL) and far-field performance of the protype are measured by an Agilent E5071Â C vector network analyzer and SATIMO SG 24 measurement system in an anechoic chamber, respectively. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a> shows the simulated and measured reflection coefficient of input port, gain, cross-polarization, AR at boresight, and measured efficiency of the protype. For <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-88-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1030" role="math" style="width: 5.829em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.228em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.17em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1031"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1032"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1033"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1034" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1035" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1036" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">&gt;</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1037" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">10</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1038" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1039"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1040"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1041" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">dB</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.13em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-88">{\rm RL} &gt; 10~\hbox{dB}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the measured impedance bandwidth is 36.0% from 0.748 to 1.076Â GHz. The proposed antenna exhibits measured peak gain of 3.1 dBic and the maximum efficiency of 67% at 0.885Â GHz with a 3-dB gain variation bandwidth of 14.9% from 0.825 to 0.958Â GHz. In addition, the measured ratio of co-polarization (RHCP) to cross-polarization (LHCP) is greater than 17.6Â dB in the band of 3-dB gain variation. The measured 3-dB AR bandwidth is 18.6% from 0.805 to 0.970Â GHz. In terms of the common frequency range for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-89-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1042" role="math" style="width: 5.829em; 13~\hbox{dB}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, 3-dB gain variation, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-90-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1054" role="math" style="width: 5.408em; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.329em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.004em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-100">yoz</script></tex-math></inline-formula> planes.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7042302/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>In addition, comparison of impedance bandwidth, AR bandwidth, peak gain, and volume to the reported RFID CP directional reader antennas are illustrated in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ I</a>. The proposed antenna not only exhibits the largest CP bandwidth for easily covering the universal UHF RFID band but also achieves the compact size of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-101-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1116" role="math" style="width: 10.153em; top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1117"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1118" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">95</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1119" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">Ã</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1120" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">100</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1121" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">Ã</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1122" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">13.6</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1123" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1124"><span style="display: inline-block; <div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>In this letter, a CP directional antenna has been proposed for universal UHF RFID handheld reader application. The four-feed network and four sequentially rotated IFAs are employed to achieve compact size and wideband. The cost is reduced by using FR-4 substrates and an air layer. For <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-102-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1129" role="math" style="width: 5.829em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.228em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.17em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1130"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1131"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1132"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1133" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1134" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1135" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">&gt;</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1136" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">13</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1137" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1138"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1139"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1140" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">dB</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.13em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-102">{\rm RL} &gt; 13~\hbox{dB}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, 3-dB gain variation, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-103-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1141" role="math" style="width: 5.408em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.868em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.81em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1142"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1143"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1144"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1145" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">A</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1146" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1147" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">&lt;</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1148" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">2</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1149" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1150"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1151"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1152" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">dB</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.13em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.003em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-103">{\rm AR} &lt; 2~\hbox{dB}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the antenna achieves the bandwidth of 14.9% and exhibits stable symmetrical directional radiation patterns with wide half-power beamwidth. The comparison shows that the design exhibits the largest CP bandwidth and achieves compact size of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-104-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1153" role="math" style="width: 10.153em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 9.132em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1009.13em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1154"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1155" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">95</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1156" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">Ã</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1157" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">100</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1158" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">Ã</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1159" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">13.6</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1160" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1161"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.68em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1162"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1163"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1164" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.685em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1165" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-104">95 \times 100 \times 13.6~\hbox{mm}^3</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Thus it is very well suited to RFID handheld reader applications.</p></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

	if(getCookie('legacyUserName')!=null)
	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>

Handheld Reader Applications","abstract":"A low-cost compact circularly polarized (CP) directional antenna is proposed for universal ultra-high frequency (UHF) RF identification (RFID) handheld reader applications. The antenna consists of four sequentially rotated inverted-F antennas (IFAs) fed by a compact four-feed network with closed-form design formulas. A prototype is implemented by FR-4 substrates and a thick air layer for the reduction of cost. For return loss (RL) &amp;gt; 13 dB, 3-dB gain variation, and axial ratio (AR) , the prototype achieves the measured bandwidth of 14.9% and exhibits stable symmetrical directional radiation patterns with wide half-power beamwidth. Compared with the reported UHF RFID directional reader antennas, the proposed structure not only exhibits the largest CP bandwidth for easily covering the entire UHF RFID band but also achieves compact size of 95 &amp;#x00D7;100 &amp;#x00D7;13.6 mm&lt;sup&gt;3&lt;/sup&gt;.","isJournal":true,"isConference":false,"dateOfInsertion":"05 June 2015","publicationDate":"2015","conferenceDate":" ","isACM":false,"volume":"14","publisher":"IEEE","isEarlyAccess":false,"isBook":false,"isEphemera":false,"isOpenAccess":false,"accessionNumber":"15209523","htmlLink":"/document/7042302/","isDynamicHtml":true,"isFreeDocument":false,"isSMPTE":false,"isCustomDenial":false,"persistentLink":"http://ieeexplore.ieee.org/servlet/opac?punumber=7727","isStaticHtml":true,"isNotDynamicOrStatic":false,"htmlAbstractLink":"/document/7042302/","isPromo":false,"journalDisplayDateOfPublication":"13 February 2015","chronOrPublicationDate":"2015","isStandard":false,"startPage":"1326","fundingAgencies":{"fundingAgency":[{"fundingId":"","fundingName":"National Basic Research Program of China"},{"fundingId":"10.13039/501100001809","fundingName":"National Natural Science Foundation of China"},{"fundingId":"10.13039/501100001809","fundingName":"National Natural Science Foundation of China"},{"fundingId":"","fundingName":"Fundamental Research Funds"}]},"openAccessFlag":"no","ephemeraFlag":"false","title":"Low-Cost Compact Circularly Polarized Directional Antenna for Universal UHF RFID Handheld Reader Applications","confLoc":"","accessionNumber":"15209523","ml_html_flag":"true","html_flag":"true","content_type":"Journals &amp;
